  840 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     73 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/641C               | * We use a traditional Bresenham run-length approach.
  841 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     74 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/641C               | * Run-slicing is possible, but the code is larger
  842 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     75 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/641C               | * and the increased cost means it's only valuable
  843 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     76 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/641C               | * for longer lines.  An optimal solution would switch
  844 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     77 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/641C               | * approaches based on line length.
  845 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     78 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/641C               | *
  846 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     79 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/641C               | * Start by identifying where x0 or x1 is on the
  847 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     80 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/641C               | * left.  To make life simpler we always work from
  848 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     81 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/641C               | * left to right, flipping the coordinates if
  849 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     82 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/641C               | * needed.
  850 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     83 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/641C               | *
  851 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     84 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/641C               | * We also need to figure out if the line is more
  852 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     85 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/641C               | * than 255 pixels long -- which, because of
  853 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     86 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/641C               | * inclusive coordinates, means abs(x0-x1) > 254.
  854 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     87 | Code        | 11 |         |    3 | 00/641C : AD 0D 60    |                 lda   in_x1l         ;assume x0 on left
  855 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     88 | Code        | 11 |         |    1 | 00/641F : 38          |                 sec                  
  856 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     89 | Code        | 11 |         |    3 | 00/6420 : ED 0A 60    |                 sbc   in_x0l         
  857 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     90 | Code        | 11 |         |    1 | 00/6423 : AA          |                 tax                  
  858 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     91 | Code        | 11 |         |    2 | 00/6424 : F0 2D       |                 beq   checkvert      ;low bytes even, check hi
  859 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     92 | Code        | 11 |         |    3 | 00/6426 : AD 0E 60    |                 lda   in_x1h         
  860 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s     93 | Code        | 11 |         |    3 | 00/6429 : ED 0B 60    |                 sbc   in_x0h

  941 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s    197 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/64B2               | * At this point we have the initial X position in
  942 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s    198 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/64B2               | * ]startxl/h, the initial Y position in ]starty,

  945 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s    201 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/64B2               | * DEC depending on the direction of movement.
  946 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s    202 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/64B2               | *
  947 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s    203 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/64B2               | * The next step is to decide whether the line is
  948 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s    204 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/64B2               | * horizontal-dominant or vertical-dominant, and
  949 |  2   FDRAW.LINE.s    205 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/64B2               | * branch to the appropriate handler.

 1404 |  3 FDRAW.CIRCLE.s     58 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/66C2               | * tables.  For an outline circle, we also plot the
 1405 |  3 FDRAW.CIRCLE.s     59 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/66C2               | * points immediately.

 2435 |  5 FDRAW.TABLES.s    200 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/7400               | * RastFill unrolled loop.  At each step we store the current
 2436 |  5 FDRAW.TABLES.s    201 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/7400               | * color value, XOR it to flip the bits if needed, and advance.
 2437 |  5 FDRAW.TABLES.s    202 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/7400               | * The caller needs to set the appropriate initial value based
 2438 |  5 FDRAW.TABLES.s    203 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/7400               | * on whether the address is odd or even.
 2439 |  5 FDRAW.TABLES.s    204 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/7400               | *
 2440 |  5 FDRAW.TABLES.s    205 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/7400               | * We can use a 3-cycle "EOR dp" or a 2-cycle "EOR imm".  The
 2441 |  5 FDRAW.TABLES.s    206 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/7400               | * former is one cycle slower, the latter requires us to
 2442 |  5 FDRAW.TABLES.s    207 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/7400               | * self-mod 40 instructions when the color changes.
 2443 |  5 FDRAW.TABLES.s    208 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/7400               | *
 2444 |  5 FDRAW.TABLES.s    209 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/7400               | * This must be page-aligned so that we can take the value
 2445 |  5 FDRAW.TABLES.s    210 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/7400               | * from the rastunidx table and self-mod a JMP without having
 2446 |  5 FDRAW.TABLES.s    211 | Comment     | 11 |         |    0 | 00/7400               | * to do a 16-bit add.  We have just enough room for the
